  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ba0427e0-cf3e-47b4-8e07-c18990cdfa52'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer10506250073932377474"><p>Jem Halliday is in love with her best friend. It doesn't matter that Kai is gay, or that he'll never look at her the way she looks at him. Jem is okay with that. But when Kai is outed online by one of their classmates, he does the unthinkable and commits suicide.</p><br/> <p>Jem is left to pick up the pieces of her broken life. Before he died, Kai left her twelve letters—one for each </p></span>
  <span id="freeText10506250073932377474" style="display:none"><p>Jem Halliday is in love with her best friend. It doesn't matter that Kai is gay, or that he'll never look at her the way she looks at him. Jem is okay with that. But when Kai is outed online by one of their classmates, he does the unthinkable and commits suicide.</p><br /> <p>Jem is left to pick up the pieces of her broken life. Before he died, Kai left her twelve letters—one for each month of the year—and those letters are all Jem has left. That, and revenge.</p><br /> <p>Although Kai's letters beg her not to investigate what happened, Jem can't let it go. She needs to know who did this, and she'll stop at nothing to find the person responsible for Kai's death. One way or another, someone is going down. Someone is going to pay.</p></span>

<div id="review_419048215" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/419048215" />
    <a title="Kirsty " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3868340-kirsty"><img alt="Kirsty " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347824234p2/3868340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/419048215?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirsty " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirsty " href="/user/show/3868340-kirsty">Kirsty </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781402292248" href="/book/show/18509624-undone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3868340-kirsty?shelf=ukya">ukya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3868340-kirsty?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3868340-kirsty?shelf=review-books">review-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3868340-kirsty?shelf=uk-author">uk-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3868340-kirsty?shelf=anti-bullying">anti-bullying</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer419048215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5017906013074993555">Undone is the third offering from author Cat Clarke and it is just brilliant. I don't think I have the words to do justice to how good this book was but I'll give it a go. <br/><br/>Undone is the story of Jem. Jem is in a bad place. She has been in love with her best friend Kai for as long as she can remember even though he was gay. She was able to live with it but when he's outed in a video on the Internet and he can't deal with it and kills himself and suddenly Jem's whole world falls apart. Jem is prac</span>
  <span id="freeText5017906013074993555" style="display:none">Undone is the third offering from author Cat Clarke and it is just brilliant. I don't think I have the words to do justice to how good this book was but I'll give it a go. <br /><br />Undone is the story of Jem. Jem is in a bad place. She has been in love with her best friend Kai for as long as she can remember even though he was gay. She was able to live with it but when he's outed in a video on the Internet and he can't deal with it and kills himself and suddenly Jem's whole world falls apart. Jem is practically at the point of being completely catatonic when she is visited by Jem's sister who gives her a series of letters from Kai, one of each month of the next year which gives her a reason to live again and the opportunity to get even with the group of popular kids she holds responsible for Kai's suicide. <br /><br />Jem decides the best way to get back at those responsible for the death of Kai is to infiltrate the popular group and take them down from within. She changes the way she looks and dresses, makes friends with the enemy and starts to date the most popular boy in school. For me it was fascinating to see the transition Jem has to make to get in with the popular crowd. It said a lot about how fragile the system of popularity within a high school system actually is. The book also really highlights the devastating way in which discriminatory bullying can affect the life of a young person and how easily someone can ruin the life of another with a few choice words or put downs. Another way in which this book really hit me was the way which you really get under the skin of Jem. You really get the sense as a reader of how emotionally raw she feels as it oozes off the page and hits you full in the face. I just found myself wanting to pick her up and do whatever possible to make everything ok again. <br /><br />The ending of the book is really poignant and is guaranteed to leave you a emotional wreck. Perfect and heart breaking at the same time. I pity the book I read next because there is no way it will compare to undone. A brilliant read which I cannot recommend highly enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5017906013074993555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/420626931?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emilija" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emilija" href="/user/show/4460175-emilija">Emilija</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4460175-emilija?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4460175-emilija?shelf=didn-t-finish">didn-t-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer420626931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15556020270251159921">I cannot believe I'm giving a one star to a Cat Clarke book. I literally can't. I even considered giving it two stars just because this is <i>Cat Clarke.</i> But no. This is a one star book for me. <br/><br/>I just expected so much more. The premise was amazing and I really looked forward to this book. I bought it when it came out and started reading it as soon as it got delivered to my doorstep, but then I opened page one and the disappointment rolled in. <br/><br/>The book is boring, to say the least. I found myself at </span>
  <span id="freeText15556020270251159921" style="display:none">I cannot believe I'm giving a one star to a Cat Clarke book. I literally can't. I even considered giving it two stars just because this is <i>Cat Clarke.</i> But no. This is a one star book for me. <br /><br />I just expected so much more. The premise was amazing and I really looked forward to this book. I bought it when it came out and started reading it as soon as it got delivered to my doorstep, but then I opened page one and the disappointment rolled in. <br /><br />The book is boring, to say the least. I found myself at times just staring into space when I was supposed to be reading. It was literally so boring that I just spaced out without even noticing it. And I know that there was probably a plot in there somewhere, but it didn't show very much. It just dragged on and was so SO painfully repetitive that I couldn't take it. Do you see how long I was reading this book for? Like five months or something. <br /><br />What do I say about the characters? I feel like there aren't any. In my eyes they were all two dimensional cardboard cutouts and that just made it worse with the whole plot that was moving slower than a snail. I just... I expected more. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15556020270251159921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_819542727" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/819542727" />
    <a title="RitaSkeeter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21914765-ritaskeeter"><img alt="RitaSkeeter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375782409p2/21914765.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/819542727?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RitaSkeeter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RitaSkeeter" href="/user/show/21914765-ritaskeeter">RitaSkeeter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21914765-ritaskeeter?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21914765-ritaskeeter?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer819542727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14114231956644997318">This is a bit of an odd book, and if I had been asked at different intervals how I would rate it, it would have fluctuated wildly. The book opens strongly, with the protagonist reeling from the suicide of her closest - and only - friend. The author elicits empathy for the characters, along with horror at the events leading to Kai's suicide.<br/><br/>From there, the book slowly starts slipping away. There are a few reasons for that. The protagonist is truly unlikeable. Whilst having sympathy and empathy fo</span>
  <span id="freeText14114231956644997318" style="display:none">This is a bit of an odd book, and if I had been asked at different intervals how I would rate it, it would have fluctuated wildly. The book opens strongly, with the protagonist reeling from the suicide of her closest - and only - friend. The author elicits empathy for the characters, along with horror at the events leading to Kai's suicide.<br /><br />From there, the book slowly starts slipping away. There are a few reasons for that. The protagonist is truly unlikeable. Whilst having sympathy and empathy for her, she treats everyone poorly, and is caught in a cycle of projecting anger, which further alienates people, that leads to further anger. When she experiences periods of happiness, she squashes those and continues on a path of self-destruction anyway.<br /><br />Further reasons I didn't like the book were the constant slut shaming from the main character; it truly was offensive and repugnant. In addition, was a strong sense of homophobia from many characters. Kai suicided due to being 'outed' in the most graphic of ways. So, the main character decided appropriate revenge for one of those she thought was responsible was to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ make everyone think he was gay  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Honestly, I found this 'revenge' storyline very difficult to stomach. I cannot imagine being so bitter and blinkered that I would cause such harm to people as this girl does. I found repulsive, and I felt dirty and revolted for reading it.<br /><br />Then, the ending. It is impossible not to mention it. The author had a chance for her character to experience growth, and instead of allowing that chose to go for cheap shocks.<br /><br />So why two stars rather than one? The secondary characters - the so called "team popular", were mostly (not all) great kids who showed a great deal of patience, respect, and forgiveness for Jem. All kindnesses that were not reciprocated by her. So, team pop were pretty awesome. <br /><br />The other reason was that this really was compulsive reading. Despite all the flaws I mentioned above, this was one of those 'one more chapter, just one more chapter' books, til before you know it is nearly 1am on a work night and you need to be up in a few short hours to get yourself and the kids ready for another day. Eek.<br /><br />So that leaves me frustrated with this author. She has great writing skill, and draws characters so very beautifully and realistically. You can hear the 'but' though right, BUT I think she needs to work on her plotting This could have been a very high quality novel if things had continued in the same vein as the start.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14114231956644997318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2555782001" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2555782001" />
    <a title="Aza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87785916-aza"><img alt="Aza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548098321p2/87785916.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2555782001?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aza" href="/user/show/87785916-aza">Aza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2555782001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11723782357416473078">"They had no idea that normal didn't exist for me anymore. NORMAL had been smashed on the rocks beneath the bridge."<br/><br/>It was an amazing book. It made me want to cry, laugh and I truly felt that the emotions had driven me crazy. Jemima Haliday is a fabulous character and she loved Kai to bits.<br/> No matter what gender he was, she still accepted him. That made this book a true masterpiece. When Kai committed suicide it made Jemima never forgive herself for that and felt as if a place in her heart was s</span>
  <span id="freeText11723782357416473078" style="display:none">"They had no idea that normal didn't exist for me anymore. NORMAL had been smashed on the rocks beneath the bridge."<br /><br />It was an amazing book. It made me want to cry, laugh and I truly felt that the emotions had driven me crazy. Jemima Haliday is a fabulous character and she loved Kai to bits.<br /> No matter what gender he was, she still accepted him. That made this book a true masterpiece. When Kai committed suicide it made Jemima never forgive herself for that and felt as if a place in her heart was scarred for life; never able to heal. She really wanted to investigate but didn't want to betray Kai. Before Kai gave in to his life, he wrote 12 letters to her and put them in an envelope, with strict rules as she had to read them each month. He did not want Jem to feel as if her life ended without him so, he gave her comfort. Jem understood. But, she always wondered, why? He left her heart-broken. And undone. No one to ever heal the gap in her heart which was getting bigger as time went on. She wanted to pay back. Pay back for what they did to him. They made his life miserable just because he was gay. He would have been living a life now but, he truly didn't have no choice and had to put his life to an end as he couldn't cope with the torture anymore. This book will be in your lives forever and you will feel the depths of the story. You will understand the struggles some young people have to face throughout their very lives. Jem was an example. She couldn't take Kai's death into consideration and her whole in her heart ripped open making her commit the unthinkable, just like Kai. She couldn't take it any more: And that's what made me cry the most. The depth of the story will tell you that life doesn't expect it the way you expected it to be. What had happened to Jem's 'best friend', Sasha, was terribly sad. Her beautiful face was utterly ruined. Without pain you would never ever know joy. This story is life-changing and it shows how young adults have to suffer in deep remorse and grief. Just because of one simple thing. And in this book that thing was: homophobia. It tells us the hidden truth of the story which is exactly the same in reality. Many people have to experience hardship throughout life like Kai. It isn't fair he commited suicide, which was truly unthinkable, for homophobic thoughts against him. He was different. Everyone is different. Even if that post hadn't been sent, he would've still felt insecure. He would have felt that he didn't feel as if he was worth living in this world where everyone is disgusted by your gender. He still would have been gone. This book really make those adamant minds change and linger into your thoughts in a poignant emotion which will only make you feel pain, pain and more pain. <br />Kai felt as if everyday wasn't a day to be worth living for. And he left everyone for good. He let fear and hurt take over him just because of those hurtful comments.<br />Cat Clarke is an amazing author who teaches us the values of things teenagers and adults have to face everyday. <br /> No one wants to feel like that. Not even you.<br />This book is unforgettable, heart-breaking and resentful. An it shocked me into heart-broken silence which will make you cry your heart out. But, it still wouldn't make a difference.<br />What's done is done for Kai.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11723782357416473078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/922075506?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/3721054-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3721054-jo?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3721054-jo?shelf=ya-thriller-mystery">ya-thriller-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3721054-jo?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer922075506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16654432989507382164">4.5 stars<br/>If you want a book that truly messes with your head.... If you want a book that has great characters who are gritty and real.... If you want a book that compels you to read it in one sitting... then this book is for you. I must in good conscience say that the book is full of foul language and sex. And typically I don't read books like that or even like them, but this book pulled me in and wouldn't let go. Cat Clarke clearly has a lot of talent, and I really enjoyed reading a book that d</span>
  <span id="freeText16654432989507382164" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br />If you want a book that truly messes with your head.... If you want a book that has great characters who are gritty and real.... If you want a book that compels you to read it in one sitting... then this book is for you. I must in good conscience say that the book is full of foul language and sex. And typically I don't read books like that or even like them, but this book pulled me in and wouldn't let go. Cat Clarke clearly has a lot of talent, and I really enjoyed reading a book that delves so deeply in the psychological realm with her characters. There aren't any flat people in this book. They are all well-fleshed out characters, and I guarantee that you won't know which one to side with. Even the main character at times is questionable in her likeability. This is a study in the psychology of revenge as well. It shows the dark side of getting even. Clarke writes with a near clairvoyant sense into the inner workings of people's thoughts and actions. I will be seeking out other books by her. I am happy this is a stand alone novel, and it truly ended the only way it could have ended. Not saying I liked the ending - just saying I understand.</span>

<div id="review_479589505" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/479589505" />
    <a title="Katie_la_geek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5067661-katie-la-geek"><img alt="Katie_la_geek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367587231p2/5067661.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/479589505?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie_la_geek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie_la_geek" href="/user/show/5067661-katie-la-geek">Katie_la_geek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer479589505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11251169003937071244">For your chance to win an ARC of this title (UK only) or a paperback of your choice (INT) visit my <a href='http://readingunderthewillowtree.blogspot.co.uk/' rel='nofollow noopener'>blog</a><br/><br/> It has taken me a long time to write this review because I have struggled to figure out what I want to say. Put simply I found this book gut wrenching, it was emotional, shocking and heart-breaking.<br/><br/><br/>Undone tackles a whole host of series subjects such as suicide and bullying and does so with great respect. Cat Clarke is an amazing storyteller and a brilliant writer. I truly commend her for takin</span>
  <span id="freeText11251169003937071244" style="display:none">For your chance to win an ARC of this title (UK only) or a paperback of your choice (INT) visit my <a href="http://readingunderthewillowtree.blogspot.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br /><br /> It has taken me a long time to write this review because I have struggled to figure out what I want to say. Put simply I found this book gut wrenching, it was emotional, shocking and heart-breaking.<br /><br /><br />Undone tackles a whole host of series subjects such as suicide and bullying and does so with great respect. Cat Clarke is an amazing storyteller and a brilliant writer. I truly commend her for taking on such serious matters and for managing to handle it with such care.<br /><br /><br />To say this is angst driven would be an understatement and there were not many reasons to smile whilst reading this. Everything seemed to get worse and worse until you get to an ending that is truly shocking. <br /><br /><br />There was one big issue I had with this book and that was Jem. I really, really disliked her. She was extremely needy and in the end was one big walking, talking cliché. She relied on her best friend Kia far too much and was almost smothering in her affection for him. When she losses him I liked her even less. Of course I felt for her but her grief soon turns to bitter rage and self-pity that gets worse as time passes. She was hell bent on revenge, no matter the cost and full of selfishness. I just wanted her to stop because she hurts anyone and everyone in her path even those who love her and don’t deserve it. <br /><br /><br />Undone is one of the most deeply affecting emotionally draining books I have ever read. It stayed with me for days after I read it and although I am glad that I did read it and finish it, it is a book I will never be able to read again.<br /><br /><b>The publisher provided me with a free copy of this book in exchange for and honest review</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11251169003937071244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer519738632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer247754252883589457">While Undone is undoubtedly an accomplished story, what sets it apart from contemporary contempories is the level of writing. Cat Clarke has a preternatural ability to create authentic teenage voices to the point that one might suspect some sort of voodoo channeling shenanigans at her writing desk. Jem’s raw, ravenous grief pours of the page, the black selfishness of all consuming loss palpable and, at times, incredibly difficult to read. The many scenes set at school will speak loudly to anyone</span>
  <span id="freeText247754252883589457" style="display:none">While Undone is undoubtedly an accomplished story, what sets it apart from contemporary contempories is the level of writing. Cat Clarke has a preternatural ability to create authentic teenage voices to the point that one might suspect some sort of voodoo channeling shenanigans at her writing desk. Jem’s raw, ravenous grief pours of the page, the black selfishness of all consuming loss palpable and, at times, incredibly difficult to read. The many scenes set at school will speak loudly to anyone who is or ever was a teen and it is this realness that makes the novel’s denouement so outstanding. The greatest triumph here, though, is that towards the end, when Jem’s seems to have lost sight of anything that matters, Clarke reels it all in. She takes the reader back to the core of her story by stating the simplest of facts succinctly, sadly and with unarguable logic. It is this, as well as the phenomenal writing and compelling story, that should place this books in classrooms and libraries around the country where it can lead those who read it to a place where it need never ring true. Read this book, it’s powerful, it’s important, and then pass it on so others can read it too. Highly, highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="247754252883589457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6365944740478650797">This was an interesting read. I thought the story was well-written, and I thought the characters were interesting. I was not expecting to like this book that much, but I really did. Throughout the story, we follow Jem as she plans on getting revenge on the people who ousted her best friend, Kai (who she also loved for many years). I thought Kai's character was explained more through the letters to Jem, but I still wish his life did not have to end. Also, through his letters, I started to see Jem</span>
  <span id="freeText6365944740478650797" style="display:none">This was an interesting read. I thought the story was well-written, and I thought the characters were interesting. I was not expecting to like this book that much, but I really did. Throughout the story, we follow Jem as she plans on getting revenge on the people who ousted her best friend, Kai (who she also loved for many years). I thought Kai's character was explained more through the letters to Jem, but I still wish his life did not have to end. Also, through his letters, I started to see Jem's insecurities come out and I also saw the potential she had as a character. I did not dislike the ending, but I thought that the ending was okay. I was upset and sad. Also, the plot twists in the book were great and kept me wanting more. I am now a fan of Cat Clarke. I can't wait to read more books by her. Overall, a great read.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_478035977" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478035977" />
    <a title="Annabelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3418018-annabelle"><img alt="Annabelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332685565p2/3418018.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/478035977?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annabelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annabelle" href="/user/show/3418018-annabelle">Annabelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer478035977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15643576503375570010">Oh I really didn't realise how much this book would hook me. It literally sucked me up and I read it in just over a day and this was a rather long proof at just over 500 pages. Undone is a very mesmerising novel about some dark subjects. There's sex, suicide, alcohol, bullying and discrimination towards gay people. There was a lot going on in this book but it was dealt with very well as Cat seems to be a master at writing realistic YA fiction. <br/><br/>Undone follows Jem Halliday whose gay best friend co</span>
  <span id="freeText15643576503375570010" style="display:none">Oh I really didn't realise how much this book would hook me. It literally sucked me up and I read it in just over a day and this was a rather long proof at just over 500 pages. Undone is a very mesmerising novel about some dark subjects. There's sex, suicide, alcohol, bullying and discrimination towards gay people. There was a lot going on in this book but it was dealt with very well as Cat seems to be a master at writing realistic YA fiction. <br /><br />Undone follows Jem Halliday whose gay best friend commits suicide due to him being bullied because of his sexuality. The first few chapters we get to know Jem and Kai's background and how they know each other. Then the inevitable happens Kai commits suicide due to a tape of him circulating online that immediately outs him. Kai was not ready to come out of the closet and can't cope with the large amount of hate mail he is getting so he finds a solution to the problem. Suicide. Kai's death sends Jem's own life spiralling downward, they were inseparable and now he's gone. Jem doesn't want to live without him, she loved him after all. She knows she must commit suicide too or the grief will never go away. Jem is counting out some pills when some letters from Jem appear, each one dated each month of the upcoming year. Jem is so startled she momentarily forgets about the pills and focuses on the letters. Kai wrote the letters in the last hours of his life and Jem will live another year so she can do that one last thing for him. In the mean time she seeks revenge on those who did this to Kai and she won't stop until she finds the culprit. <br /><br />Jem was the complete opposite of what I was expecting. I expected this sweet quiet girl, what there was, was an grumpy, Gothic, angry girl, who would just as soon punch you instead of apologise. She was so different to what I was expecting, it sent me off the rails a bit. Alas in her revenge she knows she has to change to fit in with certain people and I liked the new Jem. She smiled and enjoyed herself, she let her hair down and didn't dwell on the death of her best friend. In a way she was moving on but it was all an act. It's what she should have done but she was so hell bent on revenge that this was just an act, a facade. I felt so sorry for some of the secondary characters at the end because she was a huge bitch to them. Yes I knew she suspected a few of them but she argued with them all, I wanted to hug the others instead of her. I know this was all the pent up anger from Kai's death but I think she should have realised that things weren't so bad in this new group of friends. There was a future there waiting for her but she blew it all away with false accusations. I don't think I've felt so strongly about one character in a long while, my views and emotions were changing so rapidly even I was getting slightly confused. For a detailed character you couldn't ask for better. <br /><br />The popular group in the novel were very interesting, they weren't stuck up bitches and jocks that we're used to seeing on the TV. We have Lucas who is the popular boy who oozes self confidence but he was also so sweet, he wasn't cocky like I expected, there was a gentlemen under there somewhere. Sasha was a lovely kind girl who took Jem under her wing and what happened to her broke my heart. That was the last thing I was expecting. There are more characters who played important roles but I shall let you discover them. <br /><br />The important things that are dealt with in the novel then. We have the subject of sexuality touched upon with Kai. He was gay but he wasn't ready to reveal that to the rest of the world just yet so when it was thrust upon him, he crumbled. Then all the hate mail arrived. It really shows how other peoples actions can ruin a persons life. You must think before you act because every single person has feelings and one simply slip of yours can change their life. Oh and there's nothing wrong with being gay, you should never judge someone who is. If you suspect someone is don't shout it to the world, it's their decision if they reveal it and after all you could be wrong. You don't know what's going on in that persons mind so don't make these life changing decisions for them. There's sex too, more than I actually expected but it worked well in the story and I had no problems with it being there. There's alcohol but hey it's teenagers and parties what more can you really expect? Suicide is another key part and again you should know that if you feel that down there will always be someone to talk to and help you. You are never alone, you should always remember that. There are many important subjects in the novel and all are dealt with well. There's a lot of wisdom in this book and you can learn a lot from it. <br /><br />Undone is a heartbreaking novel. When you think that's the end and your heart has split in two, wait until the very end and then your heart will crumble. It will be so numb and shocking that there's nothing to sum up all the feelings that come to you. It is just so heartbreaking, if you're an emotional reader, do bring tissues, you're going to need a packet or two. Undone is a spectacular novel about some harsh subjects and a plot that will keep you on the edge until the end. Then you will then and truly fall over that edge and be left on the floor in a ball crying your eyes out. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15643576503375570010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_926246724" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/926246724" />
    <a title="Liviania" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1430644-liviania"><img alt="Liviania" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1218840926p2/1430644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/926246724?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liviania" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liviania" href="/user/show/1430644-liviania">Liviania</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer926246724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9815145824428341700">British author Cat Clarke's latest novel is about Jem Halliday, who has been in love with her gay best friend for awhile. Even if she didn't have that crush, he's the most important person in her life. They've been friends through thick and then, and his sunny disposition helps her keep her chin up. Of course, that's how things were.<br/><br/>Kai killed himself after someone emailed a pornographic video to the whole school, outing him in the worst way possible. (I felt kind of weird about the fact that th</span>
  <span id="freeText9815145824428341700" style="display:none">British author Cat Clarke's latest novel is about Jem Halliday, who has been in love with her gay best friend for awhile. Even if she didn't have that crush, he's the most important person in her life. They've been friends through thick and then, and his sunny disposition helps her keep her chin up. Of course, that's how things were.<br /><br />Kai killed himself after someone emailed a pornographic video to the whole school, outing him in the worst way possible. (I felt kind of weird about the fact that this storyline was clearly inspired by the real-life suicide of Tyler Clementi, but there was no author's note or afterward talking about the real case.) Jem doesn't know how she's going to survive without him, when Kai's sister gives her twelve letters: one per month, written by Kai before he killed himself. That's when Jem decides to track down whoever made the video and uploaded it and get revenge.<br /><br />The first half of UNDONE flew by. Clarke has a compulsively readable style, and Jem's emotions were raw and real. She was angry, hurt, and confused by the things that started making her feel happy. But then the book slowed down and the conclusion went totally off the rails. (For those who read it: I'm not mad about the ending. It's the climax that's really messy.)<br /><br />The revenge storyline should drive UNDONE, but it feels half baked. None of Jem's schemes are particularly clever, nor are they particularly brutal. (I like to see people get their revenge thoroughly.) Then there's the fact that she decides to base her entire course of revenge on an anonymous note. That's . . . convenient. There is literally no investigation into who did the crime, she just believes this note.<br /><br />It's sad that the plot is such a shaggy mess, because Jem is the best kind of unlikeable character. She's lashing out, and she has an impressive steely reserve. She has an interesting emotional arc. She's confused by her own instincts and ignores the ways she's grown and changes on her own. And her grief is pitch perfect. There's also some interesting commentary on popularity.<br /><br />There are seeds of a good story in UNDONE, but I can't really recommend it. The climax makes me want to bang my head into a table until I pass out. I'll stick to Clarke's other books.<br /><br />If you are LGBTQ* and struggling with thoughts of suicide, please contact the Trevor Project at 1-866-488-7386. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9815145824428341700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_515507777" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/515507777" />
    <a title="Shambhawi P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8936537-shambhawi-p"><img alt="Shambhawi P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442655888p2/8936537.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/515507777?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shambhawi P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shambhawi P." href="/user/show/8936537-shambhawi-p">Shambhawi P.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Gossip Girl, Pretty Little Liars or any other book about vicious lying b*tches</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8936537-shambhawi-p?shelf=what-the-fishitty-fish">what-the-fishitty-fish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer515507777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16087308915998841330">This book cemented a fact that I already knew.<br/><br/>Books about crazy vicious teenage girls obsessed with popularity and where everyone seems to be backstabbing anyone is NOT my cuppa tea. Books like Pretty Little Liars, Gossip Girls, and of course Undone. So this may not be a bad book but is a book I hated. <br/><br/>But by the blurb I had expected this book to be a bit different. I don't know what I was thinking.<br/><br/>In the beginning the whole Letters from Kai with missions had a whole PS I Love You vibe going on </span>
  <span id="freeText16087308915998841330" style="display:none">This book cemented a fact that I already knew.<br /><br />Books about crazy vicious teenage girls obsessed with popularity and where everyone seems to be backstabbing anyone is NOT my cuppa tea. Books like Pretty Little Liars, Gossip Girls, and of course Undone. So this may not be a bad book but is a book I hated. <br /><br />But by the blurb I had expected this book to be a bit different. I don't know what I was thinking.<br /><br />In the beginning the whole Letters from Kai with missions had a whole PS I Love You vibe going on <del>which was another book/movie that I hated</del> and I could not really make myself interested in all the moping Jem was doing. Then she started plotting revenge. It was all I could do to hold back my migraine from too much eyerolling.<br /><br />It was not that the writing was bad, it was not. But I had serious problem with the plot and the characters, especially Jem. I hated how needy she was with Kai, and though I could live with that, I couldn't live with how she made everything - including Kai's death - about herself. She was selfish and cruel and hiding behind Kai's name as an excuse and her revenge was not for Kai but for herself.<br /><br />And I couldn't get the character of Kai. At all. He was an idiot who tried to be cute. I could muster no sympathy whatsoever for him, and it is not because of my lack of trying. And his relationship with Jem was so out of the realms of acceptable.. I mean which gay dude continues to best and only friend with a girl even after knowing that she is in love with him? And which self-respecting girl acts all needy and clingy knowing that he knows how he feels and has zero chances of returning them? <del>Insanity.</del><br /><br />Being inside this girl's head made me want to slit my wrists. And no, it was not because she was "<u>suicidal</u>". <del>She totally was not.</del><br /><br />I am just the wrong person to read this book. And I DID NOT like it.<br /><br /><b> 1 Star</b>. That's all I can give it.</span>

<div id="review_2189062733" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2189062733" />
    <a title="PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8149327-pinkamy-loves-books-cats-and-naps"><img alt="PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349961865p2/8149327.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2189062733?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps " class="user" itemprop="url" name="PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps " href="/user/show/8149327-pinkamy-loves-books-cats-and-naps">PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22376782-undone">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2189062733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6352850978387960479">After a video of Kai and his secret boyfriend is sent to his classmates, he commits suicide leaving behind twelve envelops for his best friend Jem to open monthly for the next year. While the dozen letters are suppose to inspire her to live her best life, Jem plots revenge against those who she believes caused Kai’s suicide. At the end of the twelve months, Jem plots to commit suicide.<br/><br/>Jem is one of the most horrible characters I’ve read recently. Even before Kai’s death she’s simply unkind to ev</span>
  <span id="freeText6352850978387960479" style="display:none">After a video of Kai and his secret boyfriend is sent to his classmates, he commits suicide leaving behind twelve envelops for his best friend Jem to open monthly for the next year. While the dozen letters are suppose to inspire her to live her best life, Jem plots revenge against those who she believes caused Kai’s suicide. At the end of the twelve months, Jem plots to commit suicide.<br /><br />Jem is one of the most horrible characters I’ve read recently. Even before Kai’s death she’s simply unkind to everyone but Kai. She has no other friends and while railing against the popular kids, her own judgments are just as bad. She makes fun of the one girl who tries to support and befriend her after Kai’s death. The revenge she plots against the three boys she blames is cruel, almost sociopathological. She falsely outs one boy as gay, not even considering in might lead him to suicide like Kai. Whenever Jem showed glimpses of conscience, she talks herself out of doing the right (or not wrong) thing.<br /><br />I’m not certain why I loved UNDONE when I didn’t like Jem. I guess I kept waiting and hoping that she might turn herself around. I didn’t want her to hurt anyone. One of Kai’s requests was that she look after his younger (and homophobic) sister. For as devoted as Jem was to Kai, I didn’t understand why she wouldn’t nurture a relationship with her former friend. Kai was their link.<br /><br />I wish all of Cat Clarke’s books were available for Kindle. I love her writing, even when I don’t love the characters. I don’t think UNDONE will appeal to every reader, but if you’re okay with unkind narrators, you’ll probably enjoy this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6352850978387960479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer923908194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1501246971353455903">Undone is a pretty heavy and definitely compelling book that deals with teen suicide, bullying and the teen gay community. It was well written and engaging. That being said, I can't say that I really liked the story. It was a bit depressing at times. I also thought the story was a bit unbelievable. The letters were just odd and too optimistic. I had a hard time believing that someone about to commit suicide would take the time to write those letters. It just felt off to me. <br/><br/>While I could underst</span>
  <span id="freeText1501246971353455903" style="display:none">Undone is a pretty heavy and definitely compelling book that deals with teen suicide, bullying and the teen gay community. It was well written and engaging. That being said, I can't say that I really liked the story. It was a bit depressing at times. I also thought the story was a bit unbelievable. The letters were just odd and too optimistic. I had a hard time believing that someone about to commit suicide would take the time to write those letters. It just felt off to me. <br /><br />While I could understand Jam's reasons for wanting revenge and to figure out who betrayed Kai, I didn't agree with the way she went about it. I also really disliked the way the book ended. I think I just have to chalk the book up to not being a good fit for me. It has gotten great reviews, so try it out for yourself and see what you think.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1501246971353455903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3574507618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3574507618" />
    <a title="Romana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69915585-romana"><img alt="Romana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505232690p2/69915585.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3574507618?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Romana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Romana" href="/user/show/69915585-romana">Romana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69915585-romana?shelf=recommended-or-borrowed">recommended-or-borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69915585-romana?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3574507618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7674522412279834748">4 stars.<br/><br/>(<a href='https://www.doesthedogdie.com/media/708153' rel='nofollow noopener'>Here</a> are some trigger warnings. Will mention suicide in this review.)<br/><br/>First Cat Clarke book complete! Safe to say I will be more than happy to read another.<br/><br/>Jem and Kai have been inseparable since they befriended each other over their garden fence when they were just kids. Kai is the most important person in Jem's life, so when an explicit video outing Kai's sexuality gets circulated around their school, Jem is hurt almost as much her best friend. Almost. The video is too much for Kai. Su</span>
  <span id="freeText7674522412279834748" style="display:none">4 stars.<br /><br />(<a href="https://www.doesthedogdie.com/media/708153" rel="nofollow noopener">Here</a> are some trigger warnings. Will mention suicide in this review.)<br /><br />First Cat Clarke book complete! Safe to say I will be more than happy to read another.<br /><br />Jem and Kai have been inseparable since they befriended each other over their garden fence when they were just kids. Kai is the most important person in Jem's life, so when an explicit video outing Kai's sexuality gets circulated around their school, Jem is hurt almost as much her best friend. Almost. The video is too much for Kai. Suddenly Jem finds herself alone in a world that was only just bearable when Kai was beside her. When she receives an anonymous tip revealing the people behind the video, Jem makes a promise: she will avenge her best friend, and it will be the last thing she ever does.<br /><br />Let's start with Jem - a deeply flawed and often questionable protagonist and narrator who, despite her issues, I found myself warming to very quickly. I really enjoyed her honest narration and somewhat blunt descriptions and introspection. Like I said, she has a lot of problems and isn't exactly <i>likeable</i> for much of the novel, but I was still grateful for her insight and thought her perspective was definitely an intriguing one to follow.<br /><br />The premise for <i>Undone</i> was interesting, and I still remain somewhat conflicted as to whether I liked one of the main aspects: Kai's letters. Essentially, Kai infiltrates Jem's life from beyond the grave and directs and reassures her through monthly letters that he wrote her before his suicide. I was glad to see more of Kai's character this way - he is, after all, a massive part of Jem's life - but there is always something shifty about people controlling things when they aren't around anymore. Kai tries to instruct Jem on her life without him, giving her strange 'challenges' that seemed strangely out of character for him. He didn't seem like the type to want Jem to do anything she wouldn't come up with off her own back. But ok, it contributed to the rest of the plot, I guess. These challenges fade away by the novel's midway point, which I was happy about I suppose, but unfortunately the letters lost all sense of purpose after this. I understand that I'm contradicting myself here, but basically I wanted the letter to have a bit more of a <i>point</i> - to say something a bit more significant and relevant.<br /><br />Another small complaint whilst I'm here - I guessed the big reveal. This isn't usually a huge issue since I have no problem with a novel being predictable to some extents, but it annoyed me that Jem never <i>considered</i> this possibility. As a result, it's dropped on readers out of nowhere and I think Clarke missed an opportunity to unpick the situation and give us more sense of justification and explanation. Instead, everything except Jem's impulsive revenge plot is pretty much completely ignored until the novel's final moments, which lessened the impact for me.<br /><br />Having said this, I did enjoy reading the details of Jem's plot. It introduces a cast of complex and interesting characters who I liked getting to know, particularly Lucas, Stu and Sasha.<br /><br />Overall, my first Cat Clarke experience has been a positive one. <i>Undone</i> wasn't what I was expecting, but it was a pleasantly surprising read and I look forward to moving onto another of Clarke's books!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7674522412279834748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16011600633898906577">It would have been 4 stars but that ending did a fair share of damage.<br/><br/>I did not expect to like this story. I have little sympathy for suicide as a general rule since the choice is almost always in the moment over the current drama of life. But reading this was for a challenge so I dove in.   <span id="freeText16011600633898906577" style="display:none">It would have been 4 stars but that ending did a fair share of damage.<br /><br />I did not expect to like this story. I have little sympathy for suicide as a general rule since the choice is almost always in the moment over the current drama of life. But reading this was for a challenge so I dove in. And found I really liked the story and the writing style! <br /><br />I really wish Kai did not off himself. He seems like such a great guy based on the letters he sends. He knew Jem well. Although for a guy about to kill himself within a few hours they are too light-hearted and if he can get that clear headed for the letter writing he could have pulled past this if he as waited. SO in a way, the letters didn't feel real for the emotion he was supposedly feeling. Jem I have mixed emotions on. SHe has serious tunnel vision to life and what is going on. From Kai spending less time with her, the party, her own 1 year plans, revenge, etc. She just does not stop and look at the bigger picture so she annoyed me in that sense. But I also could enjoy reading about her. The other characters are not how some seem. <br /><br />All the way to the last few pages I really enjoyed the book but it is amazing how a few pages can make me want to shout "SERIOUSLY?!?!" at it.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3136809748" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3136809748" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/89494011-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542559342p2/89494011.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3136809748?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/89494011-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3136809748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4468342267765864058">TW: homophobia, suicide, slut shaming, internalised misogyny, sexual assault, child pornography, scenes of a graphic nature. <br/><br/>Before I get into why this was a hard no book for me, I will say that it was a quick and easy reader and I flew through it in a couple of hours. <br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<br/>What was this book. The plot was honestly so bad imo and didn't make any bit of sense. Kai, Jem's best friend, is filmed with a guy and this video is then sent around the school, which subsequently results in him ki</span></span>
  <span id="freeText4468342267765864058" style="display:none">TW: homophobia, suicide, slut shaming, internalised misogyny, sexual assault, child pornography, scenes of a graphic nature. <br /><br />Before I get into why this was a hard no book for me, I will say that it was a quick and easy reader and I flew through it in a couple of hours. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />What was this book. The plot was honestly so bad imo and didn't make any bit of sense. Kai, Jem's best friend, is filmed with a guy and this video is then sent around the school, which subsequently results in him killing himself. But not before he sits down and writes 12 uplifting letters to his best friend telling her how important it is to live her life (this just didn't ring true to me). At no point does anyone point out that this is child pornography; these are underage people being filmed and sent around THAT IS CHILD PORNOGRAPHY. As a result of her friend's death, Jem decides to go on a mission to get revenge on the people she holds responsible (but don't worry, she totally knows they did it and wouldn't just ruin the lives of three people for no reason... right?)<br /><br />THAT'S EXACTLY WHAT SHE DOES. Except for Stu because let's be honest, he is an utter creep and most likely would have attacked Jem if she hadn't headbutted him so that one i'm letting go, apart from the fact that Jem lies to him about being raped and I just can't even with her.<br /><br />I hated Jem. That is what this boils down to for me; she was a sympathetic character for all of 5 minutes before we learn she is actually a slut-shaming hateful person. She makes no effort with her family or people who try and reach out and offer their support. I just wanted to shake her and ask her why she acted this way; nothing terrible seemed to have happened to her in the past causing her to hate people, she just doesn't like them because. Because they're popular (and we actually later find out they're decent people). Her revenge mission makes no sense whatsoever; she gets a note (the author of said note is very obvious) and decides to, in the following order:<br /><br />1. Pretend that one of the three guys is gay and out him; exactly what happened to her friend who then killed himself....<br />2. Write all around school that one of the three guys is a rapist <br />3. Make a guy fall in love with her, fall in love with him back, have constant sex with him, feel real emotions for him.... and then say LOL JOKES but not really because i do love you forgive me?????<br /><br />IT MAKES NO SENSE. Jem at no point questions whether these people did, and her proof that they did it - she didn't want to have sex with Stu so he goes and records her friend having sex ... to spite her?? WHERE IS THE LOGIC. I completely get she wants to find out who hurt her friend but the way she goes about it just makes no sense. She becomes friends with people (and let's admit, they all actually seem to be quite decent individuals) but constantly slut-shames them in her head and thinks she's better than them, when actually she's virtually the worst. <br /><br />I didn't like the letters and it just didn't fit right for me with the story. His telling her to go and do certain things and all his encouragement, I just can't imagine him sitting down and writing these 12 letters to her.<br /><br />The ending didn't sit right for me either. We find out that it was actually his sister recording him, because she was just a tad upset that her brother was sleeping with her boyfriend. UNDERSTANDABLE but her reaction was not. Also, Kai is made out to be this super lovely person but then we find out he's been sleeping with his sister's boyfriend for weeks NOT NICE KAI. And yet Louise seems to stay with Max?? No explanation on that. Also, can someone tell me why Louise is so homophobic because her parents are utterly supportive and there's no explanation for it, apart from her childhood friends dad thinking it's a sin and he drives a BMW, so of course he knows what he's talking about. <br /><br />And Jem's big "reveal" was so laughable and cringey I just wanted to close my eyes, at no point did she question that maybe she was just a little bit wrong, and it all results in Sasha, who has been nothing but sweet if not a tad nosy, falling face first into a fire. And then Jem accidentally jumps over a railing, realising she doesn't actually want to die SHOCKER. Even at the end the people's lives she destroyed are still being nice to her and it doesn't make sense!!<br /><br />I honestly didn't expect this rant to be so long but I just hated it. I didn't find this sad at all, it just made me angry and I just wanted her to stop slut-shaming everybody.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="4468342267765864058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_532773114" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/532773114" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1053059-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574775332p2/1053059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/532773114?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/1053059-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053059-jessica?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053059-jessica?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053059-jessica?shelf=gblt">gblt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer532773114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5362971043674710995">I have to be honest - I had some major problems with <i>Undone</i>. This novel tells the story of Jemima, Jem for short. Her best friend, Kai, has just committed suicide as a result of anti-gay bullying, and she is left behind. She is at the end of her rope when Kai's sister delivers a package to her. Inside are notes, one for each month of the year, left for her by Kai. As she reads them, she decides to take her revenge on the group of popular kids she believes drove him to his suicide. Her method? To</span>
  <span id="freeText5362971043674710995" style="display:none">I have to be honest - I had some major problems with <i>Undone</i>. This novel tells the story of Jemima, Jem for short. Her best friend, Kai, has just committed suicide as a result of anti-gay bullying, and she is left behind. She is at the end of her rope when Kai's sister delivers a package to her. Inside are notes, one for each month of the year, left for her by Kai. As she reads them, she decides to take her revenge on the group of popular kids she believes drove him to his suicide. Her method? To become one of them, and hurt them from within.<br /><br />I almost didn't start this book. It seemed like it might be a message book, and I find those are often heavy-handed. But Jem seemed (at first) to be an interesting character, so I stuck with it. The whole revenge plot is basically <i>Mean Girls,</i> not that there can't be another, but I found it distracting.<br /><br />Kai is, unfortunately, a bit of a <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/MagicalQueer" rel="nofollow noopener">Magical Gay Person</a>. He comes across less of a real person than a convenient plot device. Naturally he is an expert on ladies (going so far as to give Jem a makeover from <i>beyond the grave</i>. His letters really bothered me - they didn't feel a bit like someone who was about to tragically end their life. I just didn't think that the character would have spent the time to write out chatty notes in which he gives hair and makeup advice while contemplating his own gruesome death in a few hours. In fact, I had a hard time believing his suicide at all. I know that suicide is an act that doesn't often make sense from the outside, but as someone who actually had a close friend commit suicide for similar reasons (minus the online bullying, obviously, as I am old) it didn't seem real. <br /><br />I appreciate positive portrayals of gay teens. I think it's very important for gay or questioning young people to be able to read about teens in similar situations. What I don't think is helpful? The number of times the gay characters in these books wind up dead. I would never recommend this book to a gay teen (what would I recommend? Well, I'd start with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16102490.How_to_Repair_a_Mechanical_Heart" title="How to Repair a Mechanical Heart by J.C. Lillis" rel="nofollow noopener">How to Repair a Mechanical Heart</a>. This book shows teens struggling, but also <i>living</i>. And it's funny. Sometimes I just can't read another tragic book.)<br /><br />Speaking of that, I hated the ending (ending details behind spoiler tags) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Seriously? That's the ending? I saw the twist coming from the first time Max was introduced, so I don't know how that was a shock. But I was really upset by Jem's death, though I didn't ever connect with her. It just felt like tragedy for the sake of a sad ending, and I was not down. It didn't feel organic for her character, who ended up in the same place she started, as though the middle of the book hadn't happened.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It's hard to write a negative review of a book that has a message that can't be argued with (anti gay bullying). I must mention that the writing itself was good, and I would certainly read another book by this author. It's really more Jem's story than Kai's, but I was unable to get past his character. I wouldn't recommend it, but I will seek more from the author!<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5362971043674710995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hEyTHxRNm0p2Bb7yyEbxiqNF7ZAloGdJnrfWDZ7FHsUN0oUCq1aeIXUZEQsehmRXE2q1kkp2GkRBxfKXJAoHIg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('66mpXP0nRYZhjqRX988xlouTZcZE5sMqpogZA2xQWeBiN79BQjxA7WKSC64hD6RLO7w9xCswvid5+j2Z1p9ABw==')})
  }
